She thrust her wand at him and he wasn't sure whether she was presenting it or about to hex him, but there could be no doubt that this was the real Bellatrix Lestrange.

The Goblin gulped, never in the bank's history had anyone asked to close their account. They were merged with other accounts of course, with marriages, or with deaths, but closed? Never!

Of course no-one had successfully broken in and then out before either, and while Gringotts had drafted him out of retirement, he reflected, for possibly the first time ever, that he did value his life more than his job, "of course," he said, hoping that he could claim later, that his quick thinking had prevented a run on the bank.

It had taken a little time, not least because the spells had left her vault in a state of chaos, but finally picking up the two large bags that she had shrunk her not inconsiderable wealth into, and then shrinking them further, she put them in her pocket. Her next stop was her husband's manor, he wasn‚Äôt there, and she wondered briefly if he‚Äôd been caught by the aurors, as she collected the remnants of her still viable potions ingredients; the smaller pieces of her equipment and the few vials that she had left sealed, wanting nothing else from this place she had hated.

Bellatrix imagined that by now, all the official portkey stations had been closed down, still, where she was going that hardly mattered and, wand out, she apparated to a barely noticeable side gate of the muggle Swiss Embassy. Making sure there was no-one around, and taking out a small key she always carried on her person, both for it's protection and hers, she placed the head on the elaborate ironwork and waited. Presently, a door appeared, and then opened, in the wall nearby and pulling her key away again, she walked through it.

"Madam Lestrange" a voice said courteously, as a being even shorter than the goblins, came forward through the gloom. "We are very sorry to learn of the death of your husband" he continued, and Bellatrix quashed her surprise and nodded regally. Her husband's family had banked with the Gnomes of Zurich for centuries and obviously the bank would know of his death, their ledgers would tell them.

"You will be making a withdrawal?" he asked solemnly.

"No" she replied, "a deposit". The gnome's eyes lit up as she continued, "My husband‚Äôs family always valued your bank highly and I have decided to move my funds here as well". The gnome was now visibly glowing, and she thought quickly and altered her original plan to open a separate account, "I do however request that our account, since it is no longer a joint one, be changed to the name of Black".

"Of course" the gnome replied, "it shall be done immediately, please come this way Miss Black". He escorted her to a lift in the wall, waited until they had both taken a grip on the handles placed for the purpose, and pressed the only button.

When the door opened again, it was into a vast lobby with many lifts and gnomes running here and there. "This way please", the gnome she had come with said, and she followed him to a car, much like those at Gringotts. She left her final request until she had made her deposit and got as far as saying, "My husband's key ‚Äî‚Äî" before the gnome interrupted her.

"Will not be recognised, whoever presents it" he reassured her. "We have very strict policies Miss Black, only the living, named owner of the account can access the vault. As of today only your key will be recognised."

"And official requests for access?" Bellatrix asked.

"Will be considered of course" the gnome replied, "it is required under the articles of the Magical Banking Convention, that all monetary establishments were forced to recognise before the Goblin Wars. Indeed I believe that any requests we have received since then, are still being considered."

Bella nodded, then wondered what to do next. If she was caught by the Ministry, it was likely she wold get a swift trial and the kiss, assuming the aurors didn‚Äôt kill her first. If she was found by any death eaters who had escaped, her future would likely include torture and a slow, lingering death and that was the best outcome. Her immediate thought therefore, was to head straight for her husband‚Äôs property on the Amalfi coast, as he clearly wouldn‚Äôt be needing it now. It would be perfect at this time of year and since she was already in Switzerland it wouldn't take long. She could send the mudblood an owl and a makeshift portkey from there.

Knowing that her wards on room 5 had not yet been breached however, turned her thoughts back to Hermione. The gnome, their business complete, coughed discretely and then pointed towards another standing behind a desk on the far side of the room, "just tell the porter when you wish to go back to London Miss Black,‚Äù he said "he will ensure that you get to your destination." Bella scowled at the thought, the gnome, unperturbed, bowed and, his duty done, walked away. Bella, ignoring the concern she felt for Hermione, turned and followed the small trickle of customers changing galleons into Swiss Francs, before leaving the bank via the main doors, a free woman for the first time since her wedding day.

Hermione meanwhile had stared at the spot where Bella had been standing for some time, before she even thought to get up.

The light had won.

Since she had first known of the magical world, only at the beginning of her first year at Hogwarts had she not been aware of, fighting even, Voldemort in some form, and now it was over, he was finally gone, Bella's disappearing mark testified to that. The possibilities were endless. She could finish her NEWTS; go to university or perhaps go travelling; find her parents; all the things she had put off planning for, never knowing if they might ever happen, if there was a future. Now that she knew there was...

Now there was Bellatrix. Hermione had not thought, when this had begun, that she could ever develop feelings for the woman, yet now, she couldn‚Äôt imagine not having them. The thought that Bella could be put back in Azkaban, or worse, was terrifying, and much as she loathed Divination, Hermione wished at this moment that she could see into the future.

She apparated just outside the gates of Hogwarts, unsure whether the wards had been put back up, the state of the grounds, or how many of Voldemort's followers were still around. Somewhat surprised at making it to within sight of the entrance before seeing another living soul, she wondered at the lack of security. The sole guard, a man she didn't recognise, though he was dressed as an auror, had to mean something, didn't it?

Hermione frowned, "No, why, what's happened?"

Kingsley passed her a paper he had in his hand which read, 'If you want them back alive, we require free passage out of the country. You will be contacted again.' It was signed the Knights of Walpurgis, which Hermione knew was just a tarted up way of saying death eaters.

"Who's missing?" she enquired.

"A coat hanger" Hermione replied frowning, "why?"

"And where is Bellatrix Lestrange?" he continued, not letting his wand drop.

Hermione eyed him calmly, clearly they originally thought she too had been kidnapped. As it was obvious now that she had not been, she briefly wondered at her own stupidity. Realising that until this moment, it hadn‚Äôt occurred to her that anyone else might have perceived her earlier behaviour as a little odd. "I don't know" she replied, noticing out of the corner of her eye that Mrs Weasley had started to go very red, and looked as if she was about to explode. She started moving back towards the doorway but was stopped by McGonagall's voice, "Stay where you are Miss Granger, the aurors that can be spared are out looking. Now you're back, your staying. I'll not have them catch anyone else wandering around".

Hermione turned, "but Headmistress‚Ä¶"

Hermione looked again around the room, what were left of her classmates were sitting despondently in a corner with Professor Flitwick. She noticed for the first time that his wand was in his hand, and wondered if they too had been prevented from joining the search. The others in the room were talking quietly in small groups among themselves, and Molly she noted was now looking apoplectic. ‚ÄúI was looking for Bellatrix‚Äù Hermione said in a low voice, though she would not have disturbed the patient, even if she had shouted.

‚ÄúOh? Well, I‚Äôm sorry I disturbed you,‚Äù Hermione said, turning to leave.

‚ÄúMiss Granger‚Ä¶‚Äù

‚ÄúYes?‚Äù the Gryffindor asked, turning her head back towards the bed.

‚ÄúMy sister‚Ä¶‚Äù the woman seated there stopped, and Hermione waited. There was silence for long seconds, then Narcissa shook her own head and said ‚Äúnever mind. Thank you again for today Miss Granger.‚Äù Hermione smiled in acknowledgement, then left.

On reaching the dungeons, she realised that despite all her time in the castle, she didn‚Äôt actually know where the entrance to Slytherin house was, and made her way towards the potions classroom on instinct. Unsurprisingly it was dark and empty, but as she turned to leave, the Bloody Baron came through the wall and demanded to know what she was doing, sneaking around at that time of night.

When she explained that she was trying to find the entrance to Slytherin he bristled, when she added, that she only wanted to talk to someone that was staying there, he mellowed slightly and advised that she wait until a more civilised hour. As there was nothing more she could do, Hermione sighed and returned back the way she had come, towards the Gryffindor common room and little rest.

Harry meanwhile, had walked back to the Great Hall. Most of the bodies had been claimed by relatives or taken by the aurors to the Ministry. Only one remained, at his request. Levitating it to what used to be the Slytherin House table, he set it down gently, lit candles all around and sat on a bench near the head, staring into the gloom beyond and really thinking of all that had happened. The years he had spent at Hogwarts and those he had spent at Privet Drive, Riddle, Dumbledore, Sirius, his parents and Snape.

Finally, as dawn signalled the beginning of a new day, he looked down at the man he had hated as long as he had known him, and acknowledged his debt. Blowing out the candles, he walked towards the doorway, tired but still deep in thought. It had taken him longer than it should, but most people he had finally learnt, could not be classified as all good or all bad. Dumbledore certainly couldn‚Äôt, nor Snape, nor he admitted could Sirius. He could no longer view the world or those in it as black and white, but shades of grey and perhaps Hermione, who had always been the first to tell him this, deserved the benefit of the doubt, despite every instinct he had, that told him she was crazy.

#~~~#

Hermione stirred as Harry came back through the portrait, the sound of the fat lady grumbling about all the comings and goings, softening as the door closed again behind him. Surprised to see his friend asleep on the sofa, he stopped still, but she had been nearer wakefulness than dreaming, and blinked her eyes open tiredly. ‚ÄúHarry? ‚ÄúWell, if you‚Äôre sure?‚Äù

‚ÄúUm‚Ä¶ yes‚Äù she replied in a small voice, wondering why she had not thought of that before.

Hermione held her breath and reached slowly forward, nothing happened. She rested her hand on the wall and mumbled Snape‚Äôs password under her breath, stepping back as the wall rearranged itself into a doorway. She was more immediately concerned however, with the ‚ÄúIncarcerus‚Äù that emanated from her lover‚Äôs lips, although at least it wasn‚Äôt Crucio, so they appeared to be making some progress. Had it been anyone else, she would have thought it poor comment on their relationship, that she was so used to this spell by now that she didn‚Äôt immediately panic as she was drawn back to the wall by the door, but she merely looked at Draco and said, ‚ÄúWhat‚Äôs going on?‚Äù

‚ÄúWe can‚Äôt get out‚Äù he replied, then indicated Bella ‚Äúshe was going to find you after McGonagall left, but when she tried to leave, the wards stopped her‚Äù he paused, then muttered, ‚ÄúI can‚Äôt either.‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôll be fine‚Äù she replied and tried to smile reassuringly, although as Bella was now standing directly in front of her, she wasn‚Äôt entirely sure he could see it.

Downstairs, so did Hermione. ‚ÄúAre you going to let me down now?‚Äù she enquired calmly.

‚ÄúAnd you didn‚Äôt think I should know at all?‚Äù

‚ÄúIt was this or Azkaban Bella, and I had to plead with them not to send you back there.‚Äù

‚ÄúYou didn‚Äôt think to warn me so I could just vanish into thin air? Most of the wards are still down after all.‚Äù

Hermione could feel her face draining it‚Äôs colour, ‚Äúwhen the headmistress said she could put wards in place, I thought it was a matter of moments‚Ä¶ by the time I got to you, I thought it was already done!‚Äù she explained.

‚ÄúAnd yet still you didn‚Äôt tell me anything about them‚Äù Bella said raising her voice.

‚ÄúI‚Ä¶‚Äù Hermione trailed off, it was true, she hadn‚Äôt even thought of telling her at the time, she had been so happy that Bella was staying out of Azkaban and with her, ‚ÄúI‚Äôm sorry‚Äù, she said, ‚ÄúI didn‚Äôt think‚Ä¶ I‚Ä¶‚Äù

Hermione reacted as she saw the wand twitch in Bella‚Äôs hand. Pulling frantically on the rope that bound her arms, she managed enough leverage to raise her jean clad legs, wrapping them tightly around the body in front of her and gripping her trainers together as much as she could, as the shock of the word Bella uttered coursed through them both. ‚ÄúThe wards are badly damaged Miss Granger, and I am not strong enough at the moment to cast them over large areas, or repair those in need of it. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôll get the room tidied up,‚Äù Hermione replied ‚Äúand the unforgivable was an accident,‚Äù she added, before shoving her hands behind her back and clenching her fists, as another tremor went through her.

‚ÄúMinerva, there are a lot of stupid but excusable things that technically cannot be done by accident‚Äù a voice said from the wall, ‚Äúletting a werewolf into a castle full of school children for instance.‚Äù

‚ÄúThere you are Severus‚Äù the Headmistress said as Hermione turned, and she could just make him out, in a landscape portrait of the lake, ‚Äúand I am not Albus, you cannot hold that over my head.‚Äù

Hermione saw Bellatrix staring at the open doorway, ‚Äúyou really can‚Äôt leave?‚Äù She said quietly, the full knowledge of what she had done, finally coursing through her.

Bellatrix did not speak, she simply moved over to the doorway and reached out a hand, the mere attempt to get a finger outside, had her hurtling backwards across the room and crumpling in a corner.

‚ÄúBella, no!‚Äù Hermione screamed, she went to help her up, but Bellatrix shrugged her off. Then without a word she lay down on one of the sofas and curled herself into a ball, her eyes staring unseeing at the room in front of her.

Hermione glanced at her worriedly as she tidied the room. When she had done as much as she could without a wand, she curled up on the other sofa and did the same. She did not know what was going through Bella‚Äôs mind, but her own was still full of the horror of what she had done. For all her worry of Bellatrix‚Äôs capture earlier, it was she herself who had allowed her to be caught. If she had only told her lover of McGonagall‚Äôs words, she could have apparated straight out of the infirmary to safety, certainly she would have got away somehow. Now‚Ä¶ now there was no escape, but had not everyone told her this would happen? Mrs Weasley, Mrs Longbottom, Kingsley? Everything could wait until after the rescue‚Ä¶ and after the rescue? After the rescue Bellatrix was still a wanted felon, after the rescue came trials and accusations and Azkaban, and‚Ä¶ Hermione closed her eyes, but the images still kept coming.


Draco found them both still motionless when he came back downstairs. Neither had slept.

Bellatrix knew that this had not been all Hermione‚Äôs doing, at least when she had calmed down enough to see reason. She could, after all, have stayed in Switzerland, although what would have become of Cissy then, she dreaded to think. She could have apparated from Malfoy Manor as soon as everyone was safe. Indeed, she should have done so, had she been thinking clearly, and not of her sister and the hand clasped so happily to hers. She had been surprised when McGonagall had come for them, and her guard was too far down to see the trap until it was too late. No. Saving the boy who lived did not, after all, mean saving herself.

Seeing Draco staring from one to the other of them as she lifted her head, she motioned him to be quiet and sat up. It did not matter, Hermione she found on rising fully, was not asleep.

The Gryffindor sat up as a house elf appeared with breakfast, winking in an out as fast as it was able and Draco walked over and examined the tray. ‚ÄúThere‚Äôs a note for you Granger‚Äù he said and picked it up.

‚ÄúWhat does it say?‚Äù Hermione asked tiredly.

‚ÄúMiss Granger, please come to my office at 11 o‚Äôclock. It‚Äôs signed by McGonagall.‚Äù He turned and looked at her, ‚Äúwhat happened after I left?‚Äù he asked.

Hermione shook her head and said nothing for a moment, then glancing around room asked, ‚Äúcan I borrow your wand, we‚Äôre supposed to have tidied this up, but this is the best I could do without one.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhy, where‚Äôs yours?‚Äù

Hermione sighed, ‚Äúthe Headmistress took them‚Äù then added, ‚Äúdon‚Äôt ask,‚Äù as Bella got up and walked silently to the door that led to the dormitories and went up the stairs.

‚ÄúOK‚Äù he said, then, motioning his wand in an arc around the room, he turned to her and said ‚Äúbreakfast?‚Äù as the room repaired itself.

‚ÄúI‚Äôm not hungry‚Äù Hermione said getting up, ‚Äúit‚Äôs all yours,‚Äù then she followed Bellatrix up the stairs.

Hermione found Bella lying on a bed in one of the dormitories. Not knowing if it was a good idea or bad one, she gave in to her desire and walking over, gingerly sat on the bed. There was no response and after a few moments, Hermione swung round and hitched her feet up, laying down on her side, facing away from her lover, ‚ÄúI‚Äôm sorry‚Äù she said. Bellatrix said nothing and Hermione let her be, content at the moment, just to be close. Eventually the bed shifted, and she felt an arm across her side as Bella curled into her body from behind. Hermione breathed a sigh of relief and covered the hand now on her stomach, with one of her own. When Hermione arrived at the Headmistress‚Äô office, it was not, as she had thought, about earlier that morning. First, the Headmistress moved over to her desk and picked up a copy of the Daily Prophet, ‚Äúyou‚Äôd better read this Miss Granger‚Äù she said.

#~~~#

She had been unable to talk to Kingsley at the Ministry, surrounded as he was by lackeys and members of the press. The Headmistress assured Hermione however, that he would be coming to Hogwarts later that day, and that they would both talk to her then.

‚ÄúAnd the second thing?‚Äù she asked.

#~~~#

Hermione meanwhile, had not gone back to the Slytherin common room. She had walked out of the entrance hall and into the grounds, letting her feet carry her where they would. There was no doubt in her mind that she loved Bella, but could she live with her? Even without her wand? Especially without her wand. After 25 years in Azkaban, the woman had serious captivity issues and Hermione had no illusions that it would be a bed of roses. After all, she had first hand knowledge of how Bella felt about being incarcerated here, what would make anywhere else they could live, any different?

If she did this, her head told her, then she would also be giving up her hopes and dreams. What about her NEWTS? University? Her parents? She would be putting her life on hold again and going to work for an employer she despised.

Yes there were some well-meaning employees at the Ministry, Mr Weasley for one, but there were also a lot of pompous idiots like Percy had been, and self-serving ones like Fudge. It was not what she had wanted from life.

Nothing had been, her heart told her, for the last few years, but hadn‚Äôt that changed a little with Bellatrix? She found herself longing for the days when they had been on opposite sides. It had been so easy when it has been just the two of them, now people knew and few, if any, would understand.

All her life she had tried not to care what anyone else thought of her, had tried to do what she thought was right, even if it made her unpopular, and it had. Bella had committed atrocities, had tortured, maimed, killed. Hermione flinched at the thought, she deserved prison, didn‚Äôt she? It was just that, that wasn‚Äôt the person she knew and shouldn‚Äôt everyone be given a second chance? She hadn‚Äôt killed Seamus, nor Remus, nor Tonks, Ginny owed her a life debt, the Malfoys would probably all be dead without her, and her? If Bella had obeyed her master, she would be dead too. If Bella had obeyed her master, Voldemort could have won, didn‚Äôt any of that count for anything? Obviously not, if Kingsley was convinced Bella would be sent back to Azkaban after her trial, despite it all.

Realising she had almost reached Hagrid‚Äôs hut, she quickly detoured towards the lake, unable to face the genial man‚Äôs questions in her current state of confusion. Bella would say yes, she had no choice. She would say yes and then rage later, and could she deal with that? She sighed, there was no choice and if she couldn‚Äôt convince them to let Bella stay free without these conditions, they‚Äôd have to come up with another plan.

She walked on. The Headmistress had said that few people knew Bella had been here, which meant even fewer would know she was still free. Ginny she hoped would be fine, and Harry, if not happy about her choice, seemed to at least realise it was hers to make, certainly his behaviour yesterday had been promising. Ron, however was a different matter entirely and she fervently hoped that his mother would not say anything to him about it. Would they be better in the muggle world? Bella would struggle at first, but at least she would have electricity, how would she even make herself so much as a cup of tea without a wand otherwise? But there was no time to find anywhere if she had to start at the Ministry tomorrow. Perhaps Harry would let them stay at Grimmauld Place, at least that would be familiar and Kreacher had seemed to adore Bella. No, they couldn‚Äôt do that, Ron was bound to be there often. Perhaps the Headmistress would let them stay there until she could find somewhere? But where did that leave them‚Ä¶

She stopped dead. Why hadn‚Äôt she thought of it before?

Running back to the castle she headed straight to the dungeons, opened the door to the Slytherin common room without conscious thought and walked breathlessly inside.

Then she stopped and thought for a moment. Couldn‚Äôt she try to make change happen? ‚ÄúIf I‚Äôm allowed to work where I want,‚Äù she said, ‚Äúit‚Äôll be in the Department for the Regulation and Control of Magical Creatures.‚Äù

‚ÄúReviving S.P.E.W?‚Äù The Headmaster smirked.

Much to Hermione‚Äôs surprise, Minister Shacklebolt had agreed to her terms without any argument. Although she had managed to use the headmistress‚Äô flue to catch him during an impromptu meeting with Elphias Doge, who had just been reappointed as special adviser to the Wisengemot. Side issues like Hermione‚Äôs he could do without and he cut the connection almost as soon as she‚Äôd said the words ‚Äòwe agree‚Äô, by saying, ‚Äúexcellent, see my secretary in the morning for department vacancies and the Head of the MLE for everything else.‚Äù Hermione did not argue, in fact she barely contained her squeal of happiness from her former Head of House as she pulled back into the room. The fastest, she‚Äôd already sent to Harry before she‚Äôd gone to see McGonagall.

#~~~#

‚ÄúShe isn‚Äôt going to splinch me is she?‚Äù he asked worriedly under his breath as he took out his wand.

‚ÄúOf course,‚Äù a voice growled from directly behind him, causing him to jump, ‚Äúthe Ministry has always had my welfare at heart after all,‚Äù she said and grabbed Harry‚Äôs wand arm as he gulped nervously and clutched his wand more tightly. Hermione turned her head and smiled apprehensively at Mrs Malfoy. The woman had taken her arm with a lot less menace, but she had always disliked side-along apparition, more so since she‚Äôd splinched Ron. She made a mental check of her bag, recalling that she‚Äôd put the dittany in a special pocket she‚Äôd sown near the top for easy access and then they disapparated with a pop.

Steep Holm, it turned out, was a small island in the middle of the Bristol Channel. Closer by distance to the muggle world than the wizarding one, it was nevertheless isolated from it by the brisk tidal currents and the difficult landing. Apart from brief periods, in which a few hardy squibs with substantial ministerial protection, had left it with some Victorian six gun batteries, and the remains of a Second World War air defence post, at the request of muggle prime ministers; the island had been left to the birds and the Blacks for nearly a millennium.

Since that particular family were much less disposed to worrying about muggle welfare than the rest of the wizarding world, they had added wards that not only repelled the majority of the muggles that to this day still arrived, but also altered the memories of a select few, to ones of an enjoyable, if somewhat hazy day out. That occasionally in the past, one or two of these did not make it off the island, was put down to accident, the climb being steep and the winds being strong. Though no more had actually disappeared since an outcry in the 1850‚Äôs, when several entire parties had vanished without a trace, which had forced the Ministry to get involved and rumours of smugglers to circulate.

The four of them had apparated to a landing stage below cormorant cliffs, Harry and Hermione having some trouble regaining their balance as the wind whipped around them. When she was finally steady, Hermione looked nervously towards the top. ‚ÄúWho lives here?‚Äù she thought to ask for the first time.

‚ÄúGreat Aunt Cassiopeia was the last one to live here,‚Äù Bellatrix said, as she waved them towards the steps up from the landing, all 208 of them. ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs been empty since she crossed the veil.‚Äù

‚ÄúYou couldn‚Äôt have apparated us to the top?‚Äù Harry grumbled.

‚ÄúMiss Granger, Mr Potter‚Ä¶‚Äù Mrs Malfoy called and they turned turned as Narcissa raised her head and straightened her shoulders, ‚Äúwe never gave you cause, but thank you both for everything you have done for my family,‚Äù she said formally.

If the girl returned.

#~~~#

Hermione did return several hours later with tea, milk, eggs, bread and pizza. Both the island and the house were in darkness and she cursed the fact that she‚Äôd left Bella with no means of light, and then Harry for almost convincing her to stay at Grimmauld Place. Much as places like this irked her, designed as they were to make her feel inferior, Bella was more defenceless than she was at the moment and she should not have been away for so long. The steps from the landing were steep and the wind buffeted her every step of the way, so that by the time the house came into sight, forbidding though it looked, she welcomed it.

She pushed at the door and was surprised that it opened so readily to her touch, despite Bella‚Äôs earlier statement that she had altered the wards to recognise her. ‚ÄúBella?‚Äù she called, then said ‚ÄúLumos‚Äù more quietly as the door closed behind her. She wandered through the hall and down a corridor, finding the kitchen, noticing that it was well set up for those with an army of house elves. She turned to the hearth, pointed her wand and said ‚Äúincendio‚Äù, the instant light casting shadows on the walls. Putting down her shopping, she located a kettle and filled it with water, but did not set it on the fire, choosing instead to find Bellatrix first.

Picking up the pizza and retracing her steps, she ignored the grand staircase and opened several doors before seeing faint light coming from under one further up the corridor in front of her. ‚ÄúBella?‚Äù Hermione said again as she opened the door, and then stopped in wonder.

The library in front of her was smaller than the one at Hogwarts, but appeared much more grand. Whether this was due to the intricate decoration, the ornately bound books or the glow cast by the magic lanterns, she did not know. Bella was sat in the midst of these, upright in an armchair, a book in her hand and a glass of wine on the table next to her. Hermione focused on the bottle, the neck carefully smashed to bypass the cork without spilling the wine, and came to the conclusion that what ever the situation Bella would never be entirely helpless, and that however much she loved her, she should not under estimate her.

‚ÄúI brought food,‚Äù she said as Bella shut her book, and passed her the large box to hold as she moved a chair and another small table over to the one Bella was sitting in. She lit the fire in the hearth in front of them, enjoying the increase in warmth, before turning back to see her lover peering into the pizza box, clearly unsure that what she was looking at was edible.

‚ÄúIt tastes better than it looks‚Äù Hermione said, carefully breaking off the top of the box and transfiguring it into a plate, before moving the contents on to it and doing the same with the bottom, and transferring half of the pizza to that. ‚ÄúHonestly,‚Äù she added as she saw the disbelieving look on Bella‚Äôs face. She sat, balanced one of the plates on her lap, and took up a slice, moaning with pleasure as she sunk her teeth in to it.
